**Humans**, scientifically known as _**Homo sapiens**,_ are [primates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Primates "Primates") that belong to the [biological family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_(biology) "Family (biology)") of [great apes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_ape "Great ape") and are characterized by [hairlessness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistory_of_nakedness_and_clothing#Evolution_of_hairlessness "Prehistory of nakedness and clothing"), [bipedality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bipedality "Bipedality"), and high [intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_intelligence "Human intelligence"). Humans have large [brains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_brain "Human brain")[compared to body size](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brain-body_mass_ratio "Brain-body mass ratio"), enabling more advanced [cognitive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive "Cognitive") skills that facilitate successful adaptation to varied environments, development of sophisticated [tools](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tool "Tool"), and formation of complex [social structures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_structures "Social structures") and [civilizations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civilization "Civilization").

Humans are [highly social](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sociality "Sociality"), with individual humans tending to belong to a [multi-layered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Level_of_analysis "Level of analysis") network of distinct [social groups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_groups "Social groups") – from [families](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Families "Families") and [peer groups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peer_groups "Peer groups") to [corporations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corporations "Corporations") and [political states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_(polity) "State (polity)"). As such, [social interactions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_interaction "Social interaction") between humans have established a wide variety of [values](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Value_theory "Value theory"), [social norms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norm_(sociology) "Norm (sociology)"), [languages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language "Language"), and [traditions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Traditions "Traditions") (collectively termed [institutions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institutions "Institutions")), each of which bolsters human [society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society "Society"). Humans are also highly [curious](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curious "Curious"): the desire to understand and influence [phenomena](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenomenon "Phenomenon") has motivated humanity's development of [science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science "Science"), [technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technology "Technology"), [philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy "Philosophy"), [mythology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mythology "Mythology"), [religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion "Religion"), and other frameworks of [knowledge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge "Knowledge"); humans also study themselves through such domains as [anthropology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anthropology "Anthropology"), [social science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_science "Social science"), [history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History "History"), [psychology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology "Psychology"), and [medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicine "Medicine"). As of 2025, there are estimated to be [more than 8 billion living humans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_population "World population").

For most of their history, humans were [nomadic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nomadic "Nomadic") hunter-gatherers. Humans began exhibiting [behavioral modernity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavioral_modernity "Behavioral modernity") about 160,000–60,000 years ago. The [Neolithic Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution "Neolithic Revolution") occurred independently in multiple locations, the earliest [in Southwest Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origins_of_agriculture_in_West_Asia "Origins of agriculture in West Asia") 13,000 years ago, and saw the emergence of [agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agriculture "Agriculture") and permanent [human settlement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_settlement "Human settlement"); in turn, this led to the [development of civilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cradle_of_civilization "Cradle of civilization") and kickstarted a period of continuous (and ongoing) [population growth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_growth "Population growth") and rapid [technological change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_change "Technological change"). Since then, a number of civilizations have risen and fallen, while a number of [sociocultural](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sociocultural_evolution "Sociocultural evolution") and [technological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_technology "History of technology") developments have resulted in significant changes to the human lifestyle.

Humans are [omnivorous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omnivorous "Omnivorous"), capable of consuming a wide variety of plant and animal material, and have [used fire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_of_fire_by_early_humans "Control of fire by early humans") and other forms of heat to prepare and [cook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooking "Cooking") food since the time of _[Homo erectus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo\_erectus "Homo erectus")_. Humans are generally [diurnal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diurnality "Diurnality"), [sleeping](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep "Sleep") on average seven to nine hours per day. Humans have had a dramatic [effect on the environment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_impact_on_the_environment "Human impact on the environment"). They are [apex predators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apex_predator "Apex predator"), being rarely preyed upon by other species.[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-1) Human population growth, [industrialisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialisation "Industrialisation"), [land development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_development "Land development"), [overconsumption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overconsumption "Overconsumption") and combustion of [fossil fuels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fossil_fuels "Fossil fuels") have led to [environmental destruction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_destruction "Environmental destruction") and [pollution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pollution "Pollution") that significantly contributes to the ongoing [mass extinction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holocene_extinction "Holocene extinction") of other forms of life.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-2)[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-3) Within the last century, humans have explored challenging environments such as [Antarctica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctica "Antarctica"), the [deep sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_sea "Deep sea"), and [outer space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_space "Outer space"), though human habitation in these environments is typically limited in duration and restricted to scientific, [military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military "Military"), or [industrial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industry_(economics) "Industry (economics)") expeditions. Humans have visited the [Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon "Moon") and sent human-made [spacecraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spacecraft "Spacecraft") to other [celestial bodies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celestial_bodies "Celestial bodies"), becoming the first known species to do so.

Although the term "humans" technically equates with all members of the [genus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genus "Genus")_[Homo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo "Homo")_, in common usage it generally refers to _Homo sapiens_, the only [extant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extant_taxon "Extant taxon") member. All other members of the genus _Homo_, which are now extinct, are known as [archaic humans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaic_humans "Archaic humans"), and the term "modern human" is used to distinguish _Homo sapiens_ from archaic humans. [Anatomically modern humans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_modern_human "Early modern human") emerged at least 300,000 years ago in [Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Africa "Africa"), evolving from _[Homo heidelbergensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo\_heidelbergensis "Homo heidelbergensis")_ or a similar species. Migrating [out of Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recent_African_origin_of_modern_humans "Recent African origin of modern humans"), they gradually replaced and [interbred](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hybrid_(biology) "Hybrid (biology)") with local populations of archaic humans. Multiple hypotheses for the extinction of archaic human species [such as Neanderthals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthal_extinction "Neanderthal extinction") include competition, violence, interbreeding with _Homo sapiens_, or inability to adapt to climate change. [Genes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene "Gene") and the [environment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environment_(biophysical) "Environment (biophysical)") influence [human biological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_biology "Human biology") variation in visible characteristics, [physiology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physiology "Physiology"), disease susceptibility, mental abilities, body size, and life span. Though humans vary in many traits (such as genetic predispositions and physical features), humans are among the least genetically diverse primates. Any two humans are at least 99% genetically similar.

Humans are [sexually dimorphic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex_differences_in_humans "Sex differences in humans"): generally, [males](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man "Man") have greater body strength and [females](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woman "Woman") have a higher [body fat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_fat "Body fat") percentage. At [puberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puberty "Puberty"), humans develop [secondary sex characteristics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secondary_sex_characteristic "Secondary sex characteristic"). Females are capable of [pregnancy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pregnancy "Pregnancy"), usually between puberty, at around 12 years old, and [menopause](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menopause "Menopause"), around the age of 50. [Childbirth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Childbirth "Childbirth") is dangerous, with a high risk of complications and [death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Death "Death"). Often, both the mother and the father provide care for their children, who are [helpless at birth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Precociality_and_altriciality "Precociality and altriciality").

Etymology and definition
------------------------

Further information: [Names for the human species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Names_for_the_human_species "Names for the human species") and [Human taxonomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_taxonomy "Human taxonomy")

[![Image 10](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9.png/250px-Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Carl_von_Linn%C3%A9.png)

[Carl Linnaeus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus "Carl Linnaeus") coined the name _Homo sapiens_.

All modern humans are classified into the [species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species "Species")_Homo sapiens_, coined by [Carl Linnaeus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carl_Linnaeus "Carl Linnaeus") in his 1735 work _[Systema Naturae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Systema\_Naturae "Systema Naturae")_.[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-4) The [generic name](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Name_of_a_biological_genus "Name of a biological genus")_[Homo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo "Homo")_ is a learned 18th-century derivation from Latin _homō_, which refers to humans of either sex.[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-5)[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-6) The word _human_ can refer to all members of the _Homo_ genus.[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Barras-2016-7) The name _Homo sapiens_ means 'wise man' or 'knowledgeable man'.[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-8) There is [disagreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species#The_species_problem "Species") if certain extinct members of the genus, namely [Neanderthals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neanderthal "Neanderthal"), should be included as a separate species of humans or as a [subspecies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subspecies "Subspecies") of _H. sapiens_.[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Barras-2016-7)

_Human_ is a [loanword](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loanword "Loanword") of [Middle English](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English "Middle English") from [Old French](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French "Old French")_humain_, ultimately from [Latin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin "Latin")_hūmānus_, the adjectival form of _homō_ ('man' – in the sense of humanity).[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-9) The native English term _[man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man\_(word) "Man (word)")_ can refer to the species generally (a synonym for _humanity_) as well as to human males. It may also refer to individuals of either sex.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-10)

Despite the fact that the word _animal_ is colloquially used as an antonym for _human_,[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-11) and contrary to a [common biological misconception](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_common_misconceptions_about_science,_technology,_and_mathematics#Evolution_and_paleontology "List of common misconceptions about science, technology, and mathematics"), humans are [animals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal "Animal").[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-12) The word _[person](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Person "Person")_ is often used interchangeably with _human_, but philosophical debate exists as to whether [personhood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personhood "Personhood") applies to all humans or all [sentient beings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sentient_being "Sentient being"), and further if a human can lose personhood (such as by going into a [persistent vegetative state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persistent_vegetative_state "Persistent vegetative state")) and what is the [beginning of human personhood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beginning_of_human_personhood "Beginning of human personhood").[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-13)

Evolution
---------

Main article: [Human evolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_evolution "Human evolution")

Humans belong to the biological [family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_(biology) "Family (biology)") of apes ([superfamily Hominoidea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominoidea "Hominoidea")).[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-14) The [lineage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lineage_(evolution) "Lineage (evolution)") of apes that eventually gave rise to humans first split from [gibbons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gibbon "Gibbon") (family Hylobatidae), next [orangutans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orangutan "Orangutan") (genus _Pongo_), then [gorillas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorilla "Gorilla") (genus _Gorilla_), and finally, [chimpanzees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chimpanzee "Chimpanzee") and [bonobos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bonobo "Bonobo") (genus _[Pan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan\_(genus) "Pan (genus)")_). The last split, between the human and chimpanzee–bonobo lineages, took place around 8–4 million years ago, in the late [Miocene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miocene "Miocene") epoch.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-15)[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-16) During this split, [chromosome 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromosome_2 "Chromosome 2") was formed from the joining of two other chromosomes, leaving humans with only 23 pairs of chromosomes, compared to 24 for the other apes.[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-17) Following their split with chimpanzees and bonobos, the [hominins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominini "Hominini") diversified into many species and at least two distinct genera. All but one of these lineages – representing the genus _[Homo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo "Homo")_ and its sole extant species _Homo sapiens_ – are now extinct.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-18)

[![Image 11](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Lucy_Skeleton.jpg/250px-Lucy_Skeleton.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lucy_Skeleton.jpg)

Reconstruction of [Lucy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucy_(Australopithecus) "Lucy (Australopithecus)")_,_ the first _[Australopithecus afarensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australopithecus\_afarensis "Australopithecus afarensis")_ skeleton found

The genus _Homo_ evolved from _[Australopithecus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australopithecus "Australopithecus")_.[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-19)[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-20) Though [fossils](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_fossils "Human fossils") from the transition are scarce, the earliest members of _Homo_ share several key traits with _Australopithecus_.[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-21)[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Villmoare2015-22) Due to the scant available evidence, the time of the divergence to the genus _Homo_ does not have a consensus.[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-:0-23) Some studies using [molecular clock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Molecular_clock "Molecular clock") techniques estimate the _Homo_ genus appeared 4.30–2.56 million years ago,[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-24) while others contest that some early _Homo_ species are incorrectly included in the genus and therefore put this estimate at about 1.87 million years ago.[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-:0-23)

The earliest record of _Homo_ is the 2.8 million-year-old specimen [LD 350-1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LD_350-1 "LD 350-1") from [Ethiopia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethiopia "Ethiopia"), and the earliest named species are _[Homo habilis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo\_habilis "Homo habilis")_ and _[Homo rudolfensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo\_rudolfensis "Homo rudolfensis")_ which evolved by 2.3 million years ago.[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Villmoare2015-22)_[H. erectus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo\_erectus "Homo erectus")_ (the African variant is sometimes called _[H. ergaster](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo\_ergaster "Homo ergaster")_) evolved 2 million years ago and was the first [archaic human](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archaic_human "Archaic human") species to leave Africa and disperse across Eurasia.[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-25)_H. erectus_ also was the first to evolve a characteristically human [body plan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_plan "Body plan"). _Homo sapiens_ emerged in Africa at least 300,000 years ago from a species commonly designated as either _[H. heidelbergensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo\_heidelbergensis "Homo heidelbergensis")_ or _[H. rhodesiensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo\_rhodesiensis "Homo rhodesiensis")_, the descendants of _H. erectus_ that remained in Africa.[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-26)_H. sapiens_ migrated out of the continent, gradually replacing or interbreeding with local populations of archaic humans.[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-27)[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-28)[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-29) Humans began exhibiting [behavioral modernity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavioral_modernity "Behavioral modernity") about 160,000–70,000 years ago,[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-30) and possibly earlier.[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-31) This development was likely selected amidst [natural climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_variability_and_change "Climate variability and change") in [Middle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Pleistocene "Middle Pleistocene") to [Late Pleistocene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Pleistocene "Late Pleistocene") Africa.[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-32)

The ["out of Africa" migration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recent_African_origin_of_modern_humans "Recent African origin of modern humans") took place in at least two waves, the first around 130,000 to 100,000 years ago, the second ([Southern Dispersal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Dispersal "Southern Dispersal")) around 70,000 to 50,000 years ago.[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-33)[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-34)_H. sapiens_ proceeded to colonize all the continents and larger islands, arriving in [Eurasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia "Eurasia") 125,000 years ago,[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-35)[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-36) Australia around 65,000 years ago,[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-37) the Americas around 15,000 years ago, and remote islands such as [Hawaii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands "Hawaiian Islands"), [Easter Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Easter_Island "Easter Island"), [Madagascar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madagascar "Madagascar"), and [New Zealand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand "New Zealand") in the years 300 to 1280 CE.[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-38)[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-39)

Human evolution was not a simple linear or branched progression but involved [interbreeding between related species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interbreeding_between_archaic_and_modern_humans "Interbreeding between archaic and modern humans").[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-pmid21179161-40)[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-41)[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-42) Genomic research has shown that hybridization between substantially diverged lineages was common in human evolution.[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-43)[DNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA "DNA") evidence suggests that several genes of Neanderthal origin are present among all non sub-Saharan-African populations, and Neanderthals and other hominins, such as [Denisovans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denisovan "Denisovan"), may have contributed up to 6% of their [genome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genome "Genome") to present-day non sub-Saharan-African humans.[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-pmid21179161-40)[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-44)[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-45)

Human evolution is characterized by a number of [morphological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphology_(biology) "Morphology (biology)"), [developmental](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_development_(biology) "Human development (biology)"), [physiological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_physiology "Human physiology"), and [behavioral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_behavior "Human behavior") changes that have taken place since the split between the [last common ancestor of humans and chimpanzees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chimpanzee%E2%80%93human_last_common_ancestor "Chimpanzee–human last common ancestor"). The most significant of these adaptations are [hairlessness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistory_of_nakedness_and_clothing#Evolution_of_hairlessness "Prehistory of nakedness and clothing"),[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-46) obligate bipedalism, increased brain size and decreased [sexual dimorphism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_dimorphism "Sexual dimorphism") ([neoteny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neoteny "Neoteny")). The relationship between all these changes is the subject of ongoing debate.[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-47)

[Hominoidea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominoidea "Hominoidea")(hominoids,[apes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ape "Ape"))Hylobatidae ([gibbons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gibbon "Gibbon")) Hominidae(hominids,[great apes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_ape "Great ape"))[Ponginae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ponginae "Ponginae")Pongo([orangutans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orangutan "Orangutan"))_[Pongo abelii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pongo\_abelii "Pongo abelii")_ _[Pongo tapanuliensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pongo\_tapanuliensis "Pongo tapanuliensis")_ _[Pongo pygmaeus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pongo\_pygmaeus "Pongo pygmaeus")_ [Homininae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homininae "Homininae")(hominines)[Gorillini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorillini "Gorillini")Gorilla([gorillas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorilla "Gorilla"))_[Gorilla gorilla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorilla\_gorilla "Gorilla gorilla")_ _[Gorilla beringei](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gorilla\_beringei "Gorilla beringei")_ [Hominini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominini "Hominini")(hominins)[Panina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Panina "Panina")Pan([chimpanzees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chimpanzee "Chimpanzee"))_[Pan troglodytes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan\_troglodytes "Pan troglodytes")_ _[Pan paniscus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan\_paniscus "Pan paniscus")_ [Hominina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hominina "Hominina")(homininans)_**Homo sapiens**_ (humans)

History
-------

Main article: [Human history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_history "Human history")

### Prehistory

Main article: [Prehistory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistory "Prehistory")

[![Image 12](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Early_migrations_mercator.svg/500px-Early_migrations_mercator.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Early_migrations_mercator.svg)

Overview of the peopling of the world by [early human migration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_human_migrations "Early human migrations") during the [Upper Paleolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic "Upper Paleolithic"), following the [Southern Dispersal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Dispersal "Southern Dispersal") paradigm

Until about 12,000 years ago, all humans lived as [hunter-gatherers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter-gatherer "Hunter-gatherer").[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-48)[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-49) The [Neolithic Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution "Neolithic Revolution") (the invention of [agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agriculture "Agriculture")) first [took place](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origins_of_agriculture_in_West_Asia "Origins of agriculture in West Asia") in [Southwest Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southwest_Asia "Southwest Asia") and spread through large parts of the [Old World](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_World "Old World") over the following millennia.[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-50) It also occurred independently in [Mesoamerica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesoamerica "Mesoamerica") (about 6,000 years ago),[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-51) China,[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-52)[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-53)[Papua New Guinea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea "Papua New Guinea"),[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-54) and the [Sahel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sahel "Sahel") and [West Savanna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudanian_savanna "Sudanian savanna") regions of Africa.[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-55)[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-56)[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-57)

The formation of permanent [human settlements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_settlement "Human settlement"), the [domestication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestication "Domestication") of animals and the [use of metal tools](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chalcolithic "Chalcolithic") coincided with permanent food surplus, for the first time in history. Agriculture and sedentary lifestyle led to the emergence of early civilizations.[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-58)[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-59)[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-60)

### Ancient

Main article: [Ancient history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_history "Ancient history")

[![Image 13](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg/250px-All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:All_Gizah_Pyramids.jpg)

[Great Pyramids of Giza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Giza_pyramid_complex "Giza pyramid complex"), Egypt

An [urban revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_revolution "Urban revolution") took place in the 4th millennium BCE with the development of [city-states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/City-state "City-state"), particularly [Sumerian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sumer "Sumer") cities located in [Mesopotamia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesopotamia "Mesopotamia").[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-61) It was in these cities that the earliest known form of writing, [cuneiform script](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuneiform_script "Cuneiform script"), appeared around 3000 BCE.[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-62) Other major civilizations to develop around this time were [Ancient Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Egypt "Ancient Egypt") and the [Indus Valley Civilisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indus_Valley_Civilisation "Indus Valley Civilisation").[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-63) They eventually traded with each other and invented technology such as wheels, plows and sails.[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-64)[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bodn%C3%A1r-2018-65)[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-66)[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-67) Emerging by 3000 BCE, the [Caral–Supe civilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caral%E2%80%93Supe_civilization "Caral–Supe civilization") is the oldest complex civilization in the Americas.[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-68) Astronomy and mathematics were also developed and the [Great Pyramid of Giza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Pyramid_of_Giza "Great Pyramid of Giza") was built.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-69)[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-70)[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-71) There is evidence of a [severe drought](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/4.2-kiloyear_event "4.2-kiloyear event") lasting about a hundred years that may have caused the decline of these civilizations,[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-72) with new ones appearing in the aftermath. [Babylonians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonia "Babylonia") came to dominate Mesopotamia while others,[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-73) such as the [Poverty Point culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poverty_Point_culture "Poverty Point culture"), [Minoans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Minoan_civilization "Minoan civilization") and the [Shang dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shang_dynasty "Shang dynasty"), rose to prominence in new areas.[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-74)[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-75)[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-76) The [Late Bronze Age collapse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Bronze_Age_collapse "Late Bronze Age collapse") around 1200 BCE resulted in the disappearance of a number of civilizations and the beginning of the [Greek Dark Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_Dark_Ages "Greek Dark Ages").[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-77)[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-78) During this period iron started replacing bronze, leading to the [Iron Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iron_Age "Iron Age").[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-79)

In the 5th century BCE, history started being [recorded as a discipline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historiography "Historiography"), which provided a much clearer picture of life at the time.[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-80) Between the 8th and 6th century BCE, Europe entered the [classical antiquity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_antiquity "Classical antiquity") age, a period when [ancient Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greece "Ancient Greece") and [ancient Rome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Rome "Ancient Rome") flourished.[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-81)[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-82) Around this time other civilizations also came to prominence. The [Maya civilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maya_civilization "Maya civilization") started to build cities and create [complex calendars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maya_calendar "Maya calendar").[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-83)[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-84) In Africa, the [Kingdom of Aksum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aksum "Kingdom of Aksum") overtook the declining [Kingdom of Kush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kush "Kingdom of Kush") and facilitated trade between India and the Mediterranean.[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-85) In West Asia, the [Achaemenid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire "Achaemenid Empire")'s system of centralized governance became the precursor to many later empires,[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-86) while the [Gupta Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gupta_Empire "Gupta Empire") in India and the [Han dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Han_dynasty "Han dynasty") in China have been described as [golden ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_ages "Golden ages") in their respective regions.[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-87)[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-88)

### Post-classical

Main article: [Post-classical history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-classical_history "Post-classical history")

[![Image 14](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Cleric-Knight-Workman.jpg/250px-Cleric-Knight-Workman.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cleric-Knight-Workman.jpg)

Medieval French [manuscript illustration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illuminated_manuscript "Illuminated manuscript") of the three [classes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_class "Social class") of medieval society from the 13th-century _Li Livres dou Santé_

Following the [fall of the Western Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire "Fall of the Western Roman Empire") in 476, Europe entered the [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages "Middle Ages").[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-89) During this period, [Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity "Christianity") and the [Church](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church") would act as a source of authority and education.[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-90) In the Middle East, [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam") became the prominent religion and expanded into North Africa. It led to an [Islamic Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age "Islamic Golden Age"), inspiring achievements in [architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Architecture "Architecture"), the revival of old advances in science and technology, and the formation of a distinct way of life.[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Renima-2016-91)[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-92) The [Christian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christendom "Christendom") and [Islamic worlds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_world "Islamic world") would eventually clash, with the [Kingdom of England](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_England "Kingdom of England"), the [Kingdom of France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_France "Kingdom of France") and the [Holy Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire "Holy Roman Empire") declaring a series of [holy wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crusades "Crusades") to regain control of the [Holy Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Land "Holy Land") from [Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim "Muslim").[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-93)

In the Americas, between 200 and 900 CE [Mesoamerica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesoamerica "Mesoamerica") was in its [Classic Period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mesoamerican_Classic_period "Mesoamerican Classic period"),[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-94) while further north, complex [Mississippian societies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippian_culture "Mississippian culture") would arise starting around 800 CE.[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-95) The [Mongol Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_Empire "Mongol Empire") would conquer much of [Eurasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia "Eurasia") in the 13th and 14th centuries.[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-96) Over this same time period, the [Mali Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mali_Empire "Mali Empire") in Africa grew to be the largest empire on the continent, stretching from [Senegambia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Senegambia "Senegambia") to [Ivory Coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ivory_Coast "Ivory Coast").[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-97) Oceania would see the rise of the [Tuʻi Tonga Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tu%CA%BBi_Tonga_Empire "Tuʻi Tonga Empire") which expanded across many islands in the South Pacific.[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-98) By the late 15th century, the [Aztecs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aztecs "Aztecs") and [Inca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inca "Inca") had become the dominant power in Mesoamerica and the [Andes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andean_civilizations "Andean civilizations"), respectively.[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-99)

### Modern

Main articles: [Modern era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_era "Modern era"), [Early modern period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_modern_period "Early modern period"), and [Late modern period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_modern_period "Late modern period")

The [early modern period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_modern_period "Early modern period") in Europe and the Near East (c. 1450–1800) began with the [final defeat of the Byzantine Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople "Fall of Constantinople"), and the [rise of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire").[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-100) Meanwhile, Japan entered the [Edo period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edo_period "Edo period"),[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-101) the [Qing dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qing_dynasty "Qing dynasty") rose in China[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-102) and the [Mughal Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mughal_Empire "Mughal Empire") ruled much of India.[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-103) Europe underwent the [Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance "Renaissance"), starting in the 15th century,[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-104) and the [Age of Discovery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_of_Discovery "Age of Discovery") began with the exploring and [colonizing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonialism "Colonialism") of new regions.[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-105) This included the [colonization of the Americas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas "European colonization of the Americas")[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-106) and the [Columbian Exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbian_Exchange "Columbian Exchange").[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-107) This expansion led to the [Atlantic slave trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade "Atlantic slave trade")[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-108) and the [genocide of the Americas' indigenous peoples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genocide_of_indigenous_people_in_the_Americas "Genocide of indigenous people in the Americas").[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-109) This period also marked the [Scientific Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_Revolution "Scientific Revolution"), with great advances in [mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics "Mathematics"), [mechanics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mechanics "Mechanics"), [astronomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomy "Astronomy") and [physiology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physiology "Physiology").[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-110)

[![Image 15](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Aldrin_Apollo_11.jpg/330px-Aldrin_Apollo_11.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Aldrin_Apollo_11.jpg)

[Buzz Aldrin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin "Buzz Aldrin") on the Moon during the [Apollo 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11") mission, whereupon he followed [Neil Armstrong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_Armstrong "Neil Armstrong") to become the second human to set foot on another [celestial body](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celestial_body "Celestial body")

The [late modern period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_modern_period "Late modern period") (1800–present) saw the [Industrial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_Revolution "Industrial Revolution") and [Technological Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_Revolution "Technological Revolution") bring such discoveries as [imaging technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imaging_technology "Imaging technology"), major innovations in transport and [energy development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_development "Energy development").[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-111) Influenced by [Enlightenment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment "Age of Enlightenment") ideals, the Americas and Europe experienced a period of political revolutions known as the [Age of Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_of_Revolution "Age of Revolution").[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-112) The [Napoleonic Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars "Napoleonic Wars") raged through Europe in the early 1800s,[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-113) Spain lost most of its colonies in the [New World](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_World "New World"),[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-114) while Europeans continued [expansion into Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa "Scramble for Africa")– where European control went from 10% to almost 90% in less than 50 years[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-115)– and Oceania.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-116) In the 19th century, the [British Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") expanded to become the [world's largest empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_empires "List of largest empires").[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-117)

A tenuous [balance of power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Balance_of_power_(international_relations) "Balance of power (international relations)") among European nations collapsed in 1914 with the outbreak of the [First World War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"), one of the deadliest conflicts in history.[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-118) In the 1930s, [a worldwide economic crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression "Great Depression") led to the rise of [authoritarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian "Authoritarian") regimes and a [Second World War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), involving [almost all of the world's countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II_by_country "World War II by country").[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-119) The war's destruction led to the collapse of most global empires, leading to widespread decolonization.

Following the conclusion of the Second World War in 1945, the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States")[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-120) and the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") emerged as the remaining [global superpowers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_superpower "Global superpower"). This led to a [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War") that saw a struggle for global influence, including a [nuclear arms race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_arms_race "Nuclear arms race") and a [space race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Race "Space Race"), ending in the collapse of the Soviet Union.[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-121)[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-122) The current [Information Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_Age "Information Age"), spurred by the development of the [Internet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet "Internet") and [artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") systems, sees the world becoming increasingly [globalized](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Globalization "Globalization") and interconnected.[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-123)

Habitat and population
----------------------

Further information: [Human geography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_geography "Human geography") and [Demography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demography "Demography")

Population statistics[[n 1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-126)[![Image 16](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Population_Density%2C_v4.11%2C_2020_%2848009093621%29.jpg/960px-Population_Density%2C_v4.11%2C_2020_%2848009093621%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Population_Density,_v4.11,_2020_(48009093621).jpg)

[Choropleth map](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Choropleth_map "Choropleth map") showing [Population density](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_density "Population density") (people per square kilometer) estimates by 30 arc-second grid in 2020
[World population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_population "World population")8.2 billion
[Population density](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_density#Human_population_density "Population density")16/km 2 (42/sq mi) by total area

55/km 2 (142/sq mi) by land area
[Largest cities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_cities "List of largest cities")[[n 2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-128)[Tokyo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tokyo "Tokyo"), [Delhi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delhi "Delhi"), [Shanghai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shanghai "Shanghai"), [São Paulo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo "São Paulo"), [Mexico City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico_City "Mexico City"), [Cairo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cairo "Cairo"), [Mumbai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mumbai "Mumbai"), [Beijing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beijing "Beijing"), [Dhaka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dhaka "Dhaka"), [Osaka](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osaka "Osaka")

Early human settlements were dependent on proximity to [water](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Water_resources "Water resources") and– depending on the lifestyle– other [natural resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_resource "Natural resource") used for [subsistence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subsistence "Subsistence"), such as populations of animal prey for [hunting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunting "Hunting") and [arable land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arable_land "Arable land") for growing crops and grazing livestock.[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-129) Modern humans, however, have a great capacity for altering their [habitats](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habitat_(ecology) "Habitat (ecology)") by means of technology, [irrigation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irrigation "Irrigation"), [urban planning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urban_planning "Urban planning"), construction, [deforestation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deforestation "Deforestation") and [desertification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desertification "Desertification").[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-130)[Human settlements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_settlements "Human settlements") continue to be [vulnerable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulnerability "Vulnerability") to [natural disasters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_disasters "Natural disasters"), especially those placed in hazardous locations and with low quality of construction.[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-131) Grouping and deliberate habitat alteration is often done with the goals of providing protection, accumulating comforts or material wealth, expanding the available food, improving [aesthetics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aesthetics "Aesthetics"), increasing knowledge or enhancing the exchange of resources.[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-132)

Humans are one of the most [adaptable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adaptation "Adaptation") species, despite having a low or narrow tolerance for many of the earth's extreme environments.[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Piantadosi-2003-133) Currently the species is present in all eight [biogeographical realms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biogeographical_realms "Biogeographical realms"), although their presence in the [Antarctic realm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctic_realm "Antarctic realm") is very limited to [research stations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Research_stations_in_Antarctica "Research stations in Antarctica") and annually there is a population decline in the winter months of this realm.[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-134) Humans established nation-states in the other seven realms, such as [South Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Africa "South Africa"), [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India "India"), [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia "Russia"), [Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia "Australia"), [Fiji](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiji "Fiji"), the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States "United States"), and [Brazil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brazil "Brazil") (each located in a different biogeographical realm).

Within the last century, humans have also explored the [deep sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_sea "Deep sea") and [outer space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outer_space "Outer space"). Human habitation within these hostile environments is restrictive and expensive, typically limited in duration, and restricted to [scientific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific "Scientific"), [military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military "Military"), or [industrial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industry_(economics) "Industry (economics)") expeditions.[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Heim-1991-135) Humans [have visited](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exploration_of_the_Moon "Exploration of the Moon") the [Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon "Moon") and made their presence known on other [celestial bodies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celestial_bodies "Celestial bodies") through human-made [robotic spacecraft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotic_spacecraft "Robotic spacecraft").[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-136)[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-137)[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-138) Since 2000, there has been continuous human presence [in space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_presence_in_space "Human presence in space") through habitation on the [International Space Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Space_Station "International Space Station").[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-139)

By using advanced tools and [clothing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clothing "Clothing"), humans have been able to extend their tolerance to a wide variety of temperatures, [humidities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humidity "Humidity"), and altitudes.[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Piantadosi-2003-133)[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-140) As a result, humans are a [cosmopolitan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmopolitan_distribution "Cosmopolitan distribution") species found in almost all regions of the world, including [tropical rainforest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_rainforest "Tropical rainforest"), [arid desert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert "Desert"), extremely cold [arctic regions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arctic_region "Arctic region"), and heavily polluted cities; in comparison, most other species are confined to a few geographical areas by their limited adaptability.[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-141) The [human population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_population "Human population") is not, however, uniformly distributed on the [Earth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earth "Earth")'s surface, because the population density varies from one region to another, and large stretches of surface are almost completely uninhabited, like [Antarctica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antarctica "Antarctica") and vast swathes of the ocean.[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Piantadosi-2003-133)[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-142) Most humans (61%) live in Asia; the remainder live in the Americas (14%), Africa (14%), Europe (11%), and Oceania (0.5%).[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-143)

[![Image 17](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Distribution-of-earths-mammals.png/500px-Distribution-of-earths-mammals.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Distribution-of-earths-mammals.png)

 Humans and their domesticated animals represent 96% of all mammalian biomass on earth, whereas all wild mammals represent only 4%.[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bar-On-144)

Estimates of the population at the time agriculture emerged in around 10,000 BC have ranged between 1 million and 15 million.[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-145)[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-146) Around 50–60 million people lived in the combined eastern and western [Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire") in the 4th century AD.[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-147)[Bubonic plagues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bubonic_plague "Bubonic plague"), first recorded in the 6th century AD, reduced the population by 50%, with the [Black Death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_Death "Black Death") killing 75–200 million people in [Eurasia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurasia "Eurasia") and [North Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Africa "North Africa") alone.[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-148) Human population is believed to have reached one billion in 1800. It has since then increased exponentially, reaching two billion in 1930 and three billion in 1960, four in 1975, five in 1987 and six billion in 1999.[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-149) It passed seven billion in 2011[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-150) and passed eight billion in November 2022.[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-151) It took over two million years of [human prehistory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prehistory "Prehistory") and [history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_history "Human history") for the human population to reach one [billion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billion "Billion") and only 207 years more to grow to 7 billion.[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-152) The combined [biomass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biomass_(ecology) "Biomass (ecology)") of the carbon of all the humans on Earth in 2018 was estimated at 60 million tons, about 10 times larger than that of all non-domesticated mammals.[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bar-On-144)

In 2018, 4.2 billion humans (55%) lived in urban areas, up from 751 million in 1950.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-United_Nations_Department_of_Economic_and_Social_Affairs_(DESA)-2018-153) The most urbanized regions are Northern America (82%), Latin America (81%), Europe (74%) and Oceania (68%), with Africa and Asia having nearly 90% of the world's 3.4 billion rural population.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-United_Nations_Department_of_Economic_and_Social_Affairs_(DESA)-2018-153) Problems for humans living in cities include various forms of pollution and [crime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime "Crime"),[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-154) especially in inner city and suburban [slums](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slum "Slum").

Biology
-------

### Anatomy and physiology

Main article: [Human body](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_body "Human body")

[![Image 18](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Anterior_view_of_human_female_and_male%2C_with_labels_2.png/500px-Anterior_view_of_human_female_and_male%2C_with_labels_2.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Anterior_view_of_human_female_and_male,_with_labels_2.png)

Basic anatomical features of female and male humans. These models have had [body hair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_hair "Body hair") and male [facial hair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facial_hair "Facial hair") removed and head hair trimmed.

Most aspects of human physiology are closely [homologous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homology_(biology) "Homology (biology)") to corresponding aspects of animal physiology. The [dental formula](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dental_formula "Dental formula") of humans is: 2.1.2.3 2.1.2.3, like other [catarrhines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catarrhini "Catarrhini"). Humans have proportionately shorter [palates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palate "Palate") and much smaller [teeth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_tooth "Human tooth") than other primates. They are the only primates to have short, relatively flush [canine teeth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canine_teeth "Canine teeth"). Humans have characteristically crowded teeth, with gaps from lost teeth usually closing up quickly in young individuals. Humans are gradually losing their [third molars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wisdom_teeth "Wisdom teeth"), with some individuals having them congenitally absent.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Revolution-155)

Humans share with chimpanzees a [vestigial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vestigiality "Vestigiality") tail,[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-156)[appendix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appendix_(anatomy) "Appendix (anatomy)"), flexible shoulder joints, grasping fingers and [opposable thumbs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposable_thumb "Opposable thumb").[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-157) Humans also have a more barrel-shaped chest in contrast to the funnel shape of other apes, an adaptation for bipedal respiration.[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-158) Apart from bipedalism and brain size, humans differ from chimpanzees mostly in [smelling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smelling "Smelling"), [hearing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hearing "Hearing") and [digesting proteins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digestion#Protein_digestion "Digestion").[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-O'Neil-159) While humans have a density of [hair follicles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hair_follicle "Hair follicle") comparable to other apes, it is predominantly [vellus hair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vellus_hair "Vellus hair"), most of which is so short and wispy as to be practically invisible.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-160)[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-161) Humans have about 2 million [sweat glands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweat_gland "Sweat gland") spread over their entire bodies, many more than chimpanzees, whose sweat glands are scarce and are mainly located on the palm of the hand and on the soles of the feet.[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-162)

It is estimated that the worldwide average [height for an adult human](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_height "Human height") male is about 171 cm (5 ft 7 in), while the worldwide average height for adult human females is about 159 cm (5 ft 3 in).[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-163) Shrinkage of stature may begin in middle age in some individuals but tends to be typical in the extremely [aged](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_age "Old age").[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-164) Throughout history, human populations have universally become taller, probably as a consequence of better nutrition, healthcare, and living conditions.[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-165) The average [mass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_weight "Body weight") of an adult human is 59 kg (130 lb) for females and 77 kg (170 lb) for males.[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-166)[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-167) Like many other conditions, body weight and body type are influenced by both [genetic susceptibility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_predisposition "Genetic predisposition") and environment and varies greatly among individuals.[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-168)[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-169)

Humans have a far faster and more accurate [throw](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Throw "Throw") than other animals.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-170) Humans are also among the best long-distance runners in the animal kingdom, but slower over short distances.[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-171)[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-O'Neil-159) Humans' thinner body hair and more productive sweat glands help avoid [heat exhaustion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heat_exhaustion "Heat exhaustion") while running for long distances.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-172) Compared to other apes, the human [heart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heart "Heart") produces greater [stroke volume](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stroke_volume "Stroke volume") and [cardiac output](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cardiac_output "Cardiac output") and the [aorta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aorta "Aorta") is proportionately larger.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-173)[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-174)

### Genetics

Main article: [Human genetics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_genetics "Human genetics")

[![Image 19](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Karyotype.png/250px-Karyotype.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Karyotype.png)

A graphical representation of the standard human [karyotype](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karyotype "Karyotype"), including both the female (XX) and male (XY) sex chromosomes.

Humans are, like most animals, [plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plant "Plant"), and [fungi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fungus "Fungus"), a [eukaryotic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eukaryote "Eukaryote"), and like most animals a [diploid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ploidy "Ploidy") species. Each [somatic cell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Somatic_cell "Somatic cell") has two sets of 23 [chromosomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chromosome "Chromosome"), each set received from one parent; [gametes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamete "Gamete") have only one set of chromosomes, which is a mixture of the two parental sets. Among the 23 pairs of chromosomes, there are 22 pairs of [autosomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autosome "Autosome") and one pair of [sex chromosomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex-determination_system "Sex-determination system"). Like other mammals, humans have an [XY sex-determination system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XY_sex-determination_system "XY sex-determination system"), so that females have the sex chromosomes XX and males have XY.[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-175)[Genes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene "Gene") and [environment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environment_(biophysical) "Environment (biophysical)") influence human biological variation in visible characteristics, physiology, disease susceptibility and mental abilities. The exact influence of [genes and environment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environment_(biophysical) "Environment (biophysical)") on certain traits is not well understood.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-176)[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-177)

While no humans– not even [monozygotic twins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monozygotic_twins "Monozygotic twins")– are genetically identical,[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-178) two humans on average will have a genetic similarity of 99.5%-99.9%.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-179)[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-180) This makes them more [homogeneous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_genetic_variation "Human genetic variation") than other great apes, including chimpanzees.[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-REGWG2005-181)[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-182) This small variation in human DNA compared to many other species suggests a [population bottleneck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_bottleneck "Population bottleneck") during the [Late Pleistocene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Late_Pleistocene "Late Pleistocene") (around 100,000 years ago), in which the human population was reduced to a small number of breeding pairs.[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-183)[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-184) The forces of [natural selection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_selection "Natural selection") have continued to operate on human populations, with evidence that certain regions of the [genome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genome "Genome") display [directional selection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directional_selection "Directional selection") in the past 15,000 years.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-185)

The [human genome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_genome "Human genome") was first sequenced in 2001[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-186) and by 2020 hundreds of thousands of genomes had been sequenced.[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-187) In 2012 the [International HapMap Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_HapMap_Project "International HapMap Project") had compared the genomes of 1,184 individuals from 11 populations and identified 1.6 million [single nucleotide polymorphisms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single_nucleotide_polymorphisms "Single nucleotide polymorphisms").[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-188) African populations harbor the highest number of private genetic variants. While many of the common variants found in populations outside of Africa are also found on the African continent, there are still large numbers that are private to these regions, especially [Oceania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oceania "Oceania") and [the Americas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Americas "The Americas").[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bergstrom2020-189) By 2010 estimates, humans have approximately 22,000 genes.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-190) By comparing [mitochondrial DNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MtDNA "MtDNA"), which is inherited only from the mother, geneticists have concluded that the last female common ancestor whose [genetic marker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_marker "Genetic marker") is found in all modern humans, the so-called [mitochondrial Eve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mitochondrial_Eve "Mitochondrial Eve"), must have lived around 90,000 to 200,000 years ago.[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-191)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-192)[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-193)[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-194)

### Life cycle

See also: [Childbirth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Childbirth "Childbirth") and [Life expectancy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_expectancy "Life expectancy")

[![Image 20](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Tubal_Pregnancy_with_embryo.jpg/250px-Tubal_Pregnancy_with_embryo.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tubal_Pregnancy_with_embryo.jpg)

A 10 mm [human embryo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_embryo "Human embryo") at 5 weeks

Most [human reproduction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_reproduction "Human reproduction") takes place by [internal fertilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_fertilization "Internal fertilization") via [sexual intercourse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_sexual_intercourse "Human sexual intercourse"), but can also occur through [assisted reproductive technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assisted_reproductive_technology "Assisted reproductive technology") procedures.[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-195) The average [gestation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gestation "Gestation") period is 38 weeks, but a normal pregnancy can vary by up to 37 days.[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-196) Embryonic development in the human covers the first eight weeks of development; at the beginning of the ninth week the embryo is termed a [fetus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fetus "Fetus").[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-197) Humans are able to [induce early labor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labor_induction "Labor induction") or perform a [caesarean section](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caesarean_section "Caesarean section") if the child needs to be born earlier for medical reasons.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-198) In developed countries, [infants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant "Infant") are typically 3–4 kg (7–9 lb) in weight and 47–53 cm (19–21 in) in height at birth.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-199)[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-200) However, [low birth weight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Low_birth_weight "Low birth weight") is common in developing countries, and contributes to the high levels of [infant mortality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant_mortality "Infant mortality") in these regions.[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-201)

Compared with other species, human childbirth is dangerous, with a much higher risk of complications and death.[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-202) The size of the fetus's head is more closely matched to the [pelvis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pelvis "Pelvis") than in other primates.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Pavlicev-203) The reason for this is not completely understood,[[n 3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-205) but it contributes to a painful labor that can last 24 hours or more.[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-206) The chances of a successful labor increased significantly during the 20th century in wealthier countries with the advent of new medical technologies. In contrast, pregnancy and [natural childbirth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_childbirth "Natural childbirth") remain hazardous ordeals in developing regions of the world, with [maternal death rates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maternal_death_rates "Maternal death rates") approximately 100 times greater than in developed countries.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-207)

Both the mother and the father provide care for human offspring, in contrast to other primates, where parental care is mostly done by the mother.[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-208)[Helpless at birth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Altricial "Altricial"), humans continue to grow for some years, typically reaching [sexual maturity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_maturity "Sexual maturity") at 15 to 17 years of age.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-209)[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-210)[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-211) The human life span has been split into various stages ranging from three to twelve. Common stages include [infancy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant "Infant"), [childhood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Childhood "Childhood"), [adolescence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolescence "Adolescence"), [adulthood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adult "Adult") and [old age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_age "Old age").[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-212) The lengths of these stages have varied across cultures and time periods but is typified by an unusually rapid growth spurt during adolescence.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-213) Human females undergo [menopause](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Menopause "Menopause") and become [infertile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infertility "Infertility") at around the age of 50.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-214) It has been proposed that menopause increases a woman's overall reproductive success by allowing her to invest more time and resources in her existing offspring, and in turn their children (the [grandmother hypothesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grandmother_hypothesis "Grandmother hypothesis")), rather than by continuing to bear children into old age.[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-215)[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-216)

The life span of an individual depends on two major factors, genetics and lifestyle choices.[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-217) For various reasons, including biological/genetic causes, women live on average about four years longer than men.[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-218) As of 2018[[update]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Human&action=edit), the global average [life expectancy at birth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth "Life expectancy at birth") of a girl is estimated to be 74.9 years compared to 70.4 for a boy.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-219)[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-220) There are significant geographical variations in human life expectancy, mostly correlated with economic development– for example, life expectancy at birth in [Hong Kong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong_Kong "Hong Kong") is 87.6 years for girls and 81.8 for boys, while in the [Central African Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_African_Republic "Central African Republic"), it is 55.0 years for girls and 50.6 for boys.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-221)[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-222) The developed world is generally aging, with the median age around 40 years. In the [developing world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_world "Third world"), the median age is between 15 and 20 years. While one in five Europeans is 60 years of age or older, only one in twenty Africans is 60 years of age or older.[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-223) In 2012, the United Nations estimated that there were 316,600 living [centenarians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centenarians "Centenarians") (humans of age 100 or older) worldwide.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-224)

Human life stages [![Image 21](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Baby_with_Aerobie_flying_ring.jpg/120px-Baby_with_Aerobie_flying_ring.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Baby_with_Aerobie_flying_ring.jpg)[![Image 22](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/%D0%A0%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%85%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA_%28%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%BE%29.jpg/120px-%D0%A0%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%85%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA_%28%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%BE%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:%D0%A0%D0%BE%D0%BC%D1%81%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%85%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%BA_(%D0%9C%D1%83%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%BE).jpg)[![Image 23](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Boy_in_Dar_es_Salaam_%2814453809622%29.jpg/120px-Boy_in_Dar_es_Salaam_%2814453809622%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Boy_in_Dar_es_Salaam_(14453809622).jpg)[![Image 24](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Pataxo001.jpg/120px-Pataxo001.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Pataxo001.jpg)[![Image 25](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/An_old_age.JPG/120px-An_old_age.JPG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:An_old_age.JPG)
