[![Image 26](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Baby_playing_with_yellow_paint._Work_by_Dutch_artist_Peter_Klashorst_entitled_%22Experimental%22.jpg/120px-Baby_playing_with_yellow_paint._Work_by_Dutch_artist_Peter_Klashorst_entitled_%22Experimental%22.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Baby_playing_with_yellow_paint._Work_by_Dutch_artist_Peter_Klashorst_entitled_%22Experimental%22.jpg)[![Image 27](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ethnie_dong_6511a.jpg/120px-Ethnie_dong_6511a.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ethnie_dong_6511a.jpg)[![Image 28](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Portrait_of_a_Persian_lady_in_Iran%2C_10-08-2006_%28cropped%29.jpg/120px-Portrait_of_a_Persian_lady_in_Iran%2C_10-08-2006_%28cropped%29.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Portrait_of_a_Persian_lady_in_Iran,_10-08-2006_(cropped).jpg)[![Image 29](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Punjabi_woman_smile.jpg/120px-Punjabi_woman_smile.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Punjabi_woman_smile.jpg)[![Image 30](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/HappyPensioneer.jpg/120px-HappyPensioneer.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:HappyPensioneer.jpg)

### Diet

Main article: [Human nutrition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_nutrition "Human nutrition")

[![Image 31](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Preparing_The_Feast.jpg/250px-Preparing_The_Feast.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Preparing_The_Feast.jpg)

Humans living in [Bali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bali "Bali"), [Indonesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indonesia "Indonesia"), preparing a meal

Humans are [omnivorous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omnivorous "Omnivorous"),[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-225) capable of consuming a wide variety of plant and animal material.[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-226)[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-227) Human groups have adopted a range of diets from purely [vegan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vegan "Vegan") to primarily [carnivorous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnivorous "Carnivorous"). In some cases, dietary restrictions in humans can lead to [deficiency diseases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deficiency_diseases "Deficiency diseases"); however, stable human groups have adapted to many dietary patterns through both genetic specialization and cultural conventions to use nutritionally balanced food sources.[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-228) The human diet is prominently reflected in human culture and has led to the development of [food science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Food_science "Food science").[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Crittenden-2017-229)

Until the development of agriculture, _Homo sapiens_ employed a hunter-gatherer method as their sole means of food collection.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Crittenden-2017-229) This involved combining stationary food sources (such as fruits, grains, tubers, and mushrooms, insect larvae and aquatic mollusks) with [wild game](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game_(food) "Game (food)"), which must be hunted and captured in order to be consumed.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-230) It has been proposed that humans have used fire to prepare and [cook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cooking "Cooking") food since the time of _[Homo erectus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homo\_erectus "Homo erectus")_.[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-231) Human [domestication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestication "Domestication") of wild plants began about 11,700 years ago, leading to the [development of agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_agriculture "History of agriculture"),[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-232) a gradual process called the [Neolithic Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution "Neolithic Revolution").[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-233) These dietary changes may also have altered human biology; the spread of [dairy farming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dairy_farming "Dairy farming") provided a new and rich source of food, leading to the evolution of the ability to digest [lactose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lactose "Lactose") in some adults.[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-234)[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-235) The types of food consumed, and how they are prepared, have varied widely by time, location, and culture.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-236)[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-237)

In general, humans can survive for up to eight weeks without food, depending on stored body fat.[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-238) Survival without water is usually limited to three or four days, with a maximum of one week.[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-239) In 2020, it was estimated 9 million humans die every year from causes directly or indirectly related to [starvation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Starvation "Starvation").[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-240)[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-241) Childhood malnutrition is also common and contributes to the [global burden of disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disease_burden "Disease burden").[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-242) However, global food distribution is not even, and [obesity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obesity "Obesity") among some human populations has increased rapidly, leading to health complications and increased mortality in some [developed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developed_country "Developed country") and a few [developing countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developing_countries "Developing countries"). Worldwide, over one billion people are obese,[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Haslam-243) while in the United States 35% of people are obese, leading to this being described as an "[obesity epidemic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epidemiology_of_obesity "Epidemiology of obesity")."[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-244) Obesity is caused by consuming more [calories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calorie "Calorie") than are expended, so excessive weight gain is usually caused by an energy-dense diet.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Haslam-243)

Food consumption is the first step of the [digestive process](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_digestive_system "Human digestive system"), in which humans ultimately expel [feces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_feces "Human feces") ranging in frequency from multiple times per day to multiple times per week.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-245)

### Biological variation

Main article: [Human genetic variation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_genetic_variation "Human genetic variation")

[![Image 32](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Seti1a.jpg/250px-Seti1a.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Seti1a.jpg)

A [Libyan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Berbers "Berbers"), a [Nubian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nubians "Nubians"), a [Syrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syrian_people "Syrian people"), and an [Egyptian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptians "Egyptians"), drawing by an unknown artist after a mural of the tomb of [Seti I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seti_I "Seti I")

There is biological variation in the human species– with traits such as [blood type](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_type "Blood type"), [genetic diseases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetic_diseases "Genetic diseases"), [cranial features](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_skull "Human skull"), [facial features](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_face "Human face"), [organ systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organ_systems "Organ systems"), [eye color](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eye_color "Eye color"), [hair color](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hair_color "Hair color") and [texture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hair_texture "Hair texture"), [height](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_height "Human height") and [build](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_shape "Body shape"), and [skin color](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_skin_color "Human skin color") varying across the globe. The typical height of an adult human is between 1.4 and 1.9 m (4 ft 7 in and 6 ft 3 in), although this varies significantly depending on sex, [ethnic origin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_origin "Ethnic origin"), and family bloodlines.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-246)[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-247) Body size is partly determined by genes and is also significantly influenced by environmental factors such as [diet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diet_(nutrition) "Diet (nutrition)"), exercise, and [sleep patterns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep_pattern "Sleep pattern").[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-248)

[![Image 33](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Hair_colors.jpg/250px-Hair_colors.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Hair_colors.jpg)

A variety of human hair colors; from top left, clockwise: [black](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_hair "Black hair"), [brown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_hair "Brown hair"), [blonde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blond "Blond"), [white](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_hair "White hair"), [red](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_hair "Red hair").

There is evidence that populations have adapted genetically to various external factors. The genes that allow adult humans to [digest lactose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lactose_tolerance "Lactose tolerance") are present in high frequencies in populations that have long histories of cattle domestication and are more dependent on [cow milk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cow_milk "Cow milk").[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-249)[Sickle cell anemia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sickle_cell_anemia "Sickle cell anemia"), which may provide increased resistance to [malaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaria "Malaria"), is frequent in populations where [malaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malaria "Malaria") is endemic.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-250)[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-251) Populations that have for a very long time inhabited specific climates tend to have developed specific [phenotypes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenotype "Phenotype") that are beneficial for those environments– [short stature and stocky build in cold regions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allen%27s_rule "Allen's rule"), tall and lanky in hot regions, and with high lung capacities or other [adaptations at high altitudes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High-altitude_adaptation_in_humans "High-altitude adaptation in humans").[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-252) Some populations have evolved highly unique adaptations to very specific environmental conditions, such as those advantageous to ocean-dwelling lifestyles and [freediving](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freediving "Freediving") in the [Bajau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bajau "Bajau").[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-253)

Human hair ranges in color from [red](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_hair "Red hair") to [blond](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blond "Blond") to [brown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brown_hair "Brown hair") to [black](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black_hair "Black hair"), which is the most frequent.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-254) Hair color depends on the amount of [melanin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melanin "Melanin"), with concentrations fading with increased age, leading to [grey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grey_hair "Grey hair") or even white hair. Skin color can range from [darkest brown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dark_skin "Dark skin") to [lightest peach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Light_skin "Light skin"), or even nearly white or colorless in cases of [albinism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albinism "Albinism").[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-roberts1-255) It tends to vary [clinally](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clinal_variation "Clinal variation") and generally correlates with the level of [ultraviolet radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultraviolet "Ultraviolet") in a particular geographic area, with darker skin mostly around the equator.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-256) Skin darkening may have evolved as protection against ultraviolet solar radiation.[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-257) Light skin pigmentation protects against depletion of [vitamin D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vitamin_D "Vitamin D"), which requires [sunlight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sunlight "Sunlight") to make.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-258) Human skin also has a capacity to darken (tan) in response to exposure to ultraviolet radiation.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-259)[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-260)

There is relatively little variation between human geographical populations, and most of the variation that occurs is at the individual level.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-roberts1-255)[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-261)[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-262) Much of human variation is continuous, often with no clear points of demarcation.[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-263)[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-264)[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-265)[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-266) Genetic data shows that no matter how population groups are defined, two people from the same population group are almost as different from each other as two people from any two different population groups.[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-267)[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-268)[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-269) Dark-skinned populations that are found in Africa, Australia, and South Asia are not closely related to each other.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-270)[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-271)

Genetic research has demonstrated that human populations native to the [African continent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_continent "African continent") are the most genetically diverse[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-272) and genetic diversity decreases with migratory distance from Africa, possibly the result of [bottlenecks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_bottleneck "Evolutionary bottleneck") during human migration.[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-273)[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-274) These non-African populations acquired new genetic inputs from local [admixture with archaic populations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interbreeding_between_archaic_and_modern_humans "Interbreeding between archaic and modern humans") and have much greater variation from Neanderthals and [Denisovans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denisovans "Denisovans") than is found in Africa,[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bergstrom2020-189) though Neanderthal admixture into African populations may be underestimated.[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-275) Furthermore, recent studies have found that populations in [sub-Saharan Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa "Sub-Saharan Africa"), and particularly [West Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Africa "West Africa"), have ancestral genetic variation which predates modern humans and has been lost in most non-African populations. Some of this ancestry is thought to originate from admixture with an [unknown archaic hominin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interbreeding_between_archaic_and_modern_humans#Archaic_African_hominins "Interbreeding between archaic and modern humans") that diverged before the split of Neanderthals and modern humans.[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-276)[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-277)

Humans are a [gonochoric](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gonochorism "Gonochorism") species, meaning they are divided into male and female [sexes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex "Sex").[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-278)[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-279)[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-280) The greatest degree of genetic [variation exists between males and females](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex_differences_in_humans "Sex differences in humans"). While the [nucleotide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleotide_diversity "Nucleotide diversity") genetic variation of individuals of the same sex across global populations is no greater than 0.1%–0.5%, the genetic difference between [males](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man "Man") and [females](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woman "Woman") is between 1% and 2%. Males on average are 15% heavier and 15 cm (6 in) taller than females.[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-281)[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-282) On average, men have about 40–50% more upper-body strength and 20–30% more lower-body strength than women at the same weight, due to higher amounts of muscle and larger muscle fibers.[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-283) Women generally have a higher [body fat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Body_fat "Body fat") percentage than men.[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-284) Women have [lighter skin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_skin_color#Sexual_dimorphism "Human skin color") than men of the same population; this has been explained by a higher need for vitamin D in females during pregnancy and [lactation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lactation "Lactation").[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-285) As there are chromosomal differences between females and males, some X and Y chromosome-related conditions and [disorders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disease "Disease") only affect either men or women.[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-286) After allowing for body weight and volume, the male voice is usually an [octave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Octave "Octave") deeper than the female voice.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-287) Women have a [longer life span](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sex_differences_in_longevity "Sex differences in longevity") in almost every population around the world.[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-288) There are [intersex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intersex "Intersex") conditions in the human population, however these are rare.[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-289)[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-290)

Psychology
----------

Main article: [Psychology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology "Psychology")

[![Image 34](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/NIA_human_brain_drawing.jpg/250px-NIA_human_brain_drawing.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NIA_human_brain_drawing.jpg)

Drawing of the [human brain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_brain "Human brain"), showing several important structures

The [human brain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_brain "Human brain"), the focal point of the [central nervous system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_nervous_system "Central nervous system") in humans, controls the [peripheral nervous system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peripheral_nervous_system "Peripheral nervous system"). In addition to controlling "lower", involuntary, or primarily [autonomic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autonomic_nervous_system "Autonomic nervous system") activities such as [respiration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Respiration_(physiology) "Respiration (physiology)") and [digestion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digestion "Digestion"), it is also the locus of "higher" order functioning such as [thought](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thought "Thought"), [reasoning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reason "Reason"), and [abstraction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abstraction "Abstraction").[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-291) These [cognitive processes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_function "Mental function") constitute the [mind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mind "Mind"), and, along with their [behavioral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behavior "Behavior") consequences, are studied in the field of [psychology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology "Psychology").

Humans have a larger and more developed [prefrontal cortex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prefrontal_cortex "Prefrontal cortex") than other primates, the region of the brain associated with higher [cognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognition "Cognition").[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-292)[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-293) This has led humans to proclaim themselves to be more intelligent than any other known species.[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-294) Objectively defining intelligence is difficult, with other animals adapting senses and excelling in areas that humans are unable to.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-295)

There are some traits that, although not strictly unique, do set humans apart from other animals.[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-296) Humans may be the only animals who have [episodic memory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Episodic_memory#In_animals "Episodic memory") and who can engage in "[mental time travel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_time_travel#Evolution_and_human_uniqueness "Mental time travel")".[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-297) Even compared with other social animals, humans have an unusually high degree of flexibility in their facial expressions.[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-298) Humans are the only animals known to cry emotional tears.[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-299) Humans are one of the few animals able to self-recognize in [mirror tests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mirror_test "Mirror test")[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-300) and there is also debate over to what extent humans are the only animals with a [theory of mind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theory_of_mind "Theory of mind").[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-301)[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-302)

### Sleep and dreaming

Main articles: [Sleep](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep "Sleep") and [Dream](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dream "Dream")

Humans are generally [diurnal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diurnality "Diurnality"). The average sleep requirement is between seven and nine hours per day for an adult and nine to ten hours per day for a child; elderly people usually sleep for six to seven hours. Having less sleep than this is common among humans, even though [sleep deprivation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sleep_deprivation "Sleep deprivation") can have negative health effects. A sustained restriction of adult sleep to four hours per day has been shown to correlate with changes in physiology and mental state, including reduced memory, fatigue, aggression, and bodily discomfort.[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-303)

During sleep humans dream, where they experience sensory images and sounds. Dreaming is stimulated by the [pons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pons "Pons") and mostly occurs during the [REM phase of sleep](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/REM_phase_of_sleep "REM phase of sleep").[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-304) The length of a dream can vary, from a few seconds up to 30 minutes.[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-305) Humans have three to five dreams per night, and some may have up to seven.[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-306) Dreamers are more likely to remember the dream if awakened during the REM phase. The events in dreams are generally outside the control of the dreamer, with the exception of [lucid dreaming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucid_dream "Lucid dream"), where the dreamer is [self-aware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-aware "Self-aware").[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-307) Dreams can at times make a [creative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creativity "Creativity") thought occur or give a sense of [inspiration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artistic_inspiration "Artistic inspiration").[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-308)

### Consciousness and thought

Main articles: [Consciousness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consciousness "Consciousness") and [Cognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognition "Cognition")

Human consciousness, at its simplest, is [sentience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sentience "Sentience") or [awareness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Awareness "Awareness") of internal or external existence.[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-309) Despite centuries of analyses, definitions, explanations and debates by philosophers and scientists, the underlying nature of consciousness remains enigmatic and poorly understood,[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-310) being "at once the most familiar and most mysterious aspect of our lives".[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-311) The only widely agreed notion about the topic is the intuition that it exists.[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-312) Opinions differ about what exactly needs to be studied and explained as consciousness. Some philosophers divide consciousness into phenomenal consciousness, which is sensory experience itself, and access consciousness, which can be used for reasoning or directly controlling actions.[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-313) It is sometimes synonymous with 'the mind', and at other times, an aspect of it. Historically it is associated with [introspection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Introspection "Introspection"), private [thought](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thought "Thought"), [imagination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imagination "Imagination") and [volition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volition_(psychology) "Volition (psychology)").[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-314) It now often includes some kind of [experience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Experience "Experience"), [cognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognition "Cognition"), [feeling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feeling "Feeling") or [perception](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perception "Perception"). It may be 'awareness', or '[awareness of awareness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meta-cognition "Meta-cognition")', or [self-awareness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-awareness "Self-awareness").[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-315) There might be different levels or [orders of consciousness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Higher-order_theories_of_consciousness "Higher-order theories of consciousness"),[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-316) or different kinds of consciousness, or just one kind with different features.[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-317)

The process of acquiring knowledge and understanding through thought, experience, and the senses is known as cognition.[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-318) The human brain [perceives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perception "Perception") the external world through the [senses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sense "Sense"), and each individual human is influenced greatly by his or her experiences, leading to [subjective](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subjectivity "Subjectivity") views of [existence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Existence "Existence") and the passage of time.[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-319) The nature of thought is central to psychology and related fields. [Cognitive psychology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_psychology "Cognitive psychology") studies [cognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognition "Cognition"), the [mental processes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mental_function "Mental function") underlying behavior.[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-320) Largely focusing on the development of the human mind through the life span, [developmental psychology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developmental_psychology "Developmental psychology") seeks to understand how people come to perceive, understand, and act within the world and how these processes change as they age.[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-321)[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-322) This may focus on intellectual, cognitive, neural, social, or [moral development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moral_development "Moral development"). [Psychologists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychologists "Psychologists") have developed intelligence tests and the concept of [intelligence quotient](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intelligence_quotient "Intelligence quotient") in order to assess the relative intelligence of human beings and study its [distribution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Distribution_(mathematics) "Distribution (mathematics)") among population.[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-323)

### Motivation and emotion

Main articles: [Motivation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Motivation "Motivation") and [Emotion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emotion "Emotion")

[![Image 35](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Plate_depicting_emotions_of_grief_from_Charles_Darwin%27s_book_The_Expression_of_the_Emotions.jpg/250px-Plate_depicting_emotions_of_grief_from_Charles_Darwin%27s_book_The_Expression_of_the_Emotions.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Plate_depicting_emotions_of_grief_from_Charles_Darwin%27s_book_The_Expression_of_the_Emotions.jpg)

Illustration of grief from [Charles Darwin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Darwin "Charles Darwin")'s 1872 book _[The Expression of the Emotions in Man and Animals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Expression\_of\_the\_Emotions\_in\_Man\_and\_Animals "The Expression of the Emotions in Man and Animals")_

Human motivation is not yet wholly understood. From a psychological perspective, [Maslow's hierarchy of needs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maslow%27s_hierarchy_of_needs "Maslow's hierarchy of needs") is a well-established theory that can be defined as the process of satisfying certain needs in ascending order of complexity.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-324) From a more general, philosophical perspective, human motivation can be defined as a commitment to, or withdrawal from, various goals requiring the application of human ability. Furthermore, [incentive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incentive "Incentive") and [preference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Preference "Preference") are both factors, as are any perceived links between incentives and preferences. [Volition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volition_(psychology) "Volition (psychology)") may also be involved, in which case willpower is also a factor. Ideally, both motivation and volition ensure the selection, striving for, and [realization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Realisation_(metrology) "Realisation (metrology)") of goals in an optimal manner, a [function](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_(biology) "Function (biology)") beginning in childhood and continuing throughout a lifetime in a process known as [socialization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialization "Socialization").[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-325)

Emotions are [biological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological "Biological") states associated with the nervous system[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-326)[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-327) brought on by [neurophysiological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neurophysiology "Neurophysiology") changes variously associated with thoughts, feelings, behavioral responses, and a degree of [pleasure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pleasure "Pleasure") or [displeasure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suffering "Suffering").[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-328)[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-329) They are often [intertwined](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reciprocal_influence "Reciprocal influence") with [mood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mood_(psychology) "Mood (psychology)"), [temperament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temperament "Temperament"), [personality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personality_psychology "Personality psychology"), [disposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disposition "Disposition"), [creativity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Creativity "Creativity"),[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-330) and motivation. Emotion has a significant influence on human behavior and their ability to learn.[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-331) Acting on extreme or uncontrolled emotions can lead to social disorder and crime,[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-332) with studies showing criminals may have a lower [emotional intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emotional_intelligence "Emotional intelligence") than normal.[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-333)

Emotional experiences perceived as [pleasant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pleasure "Pleasure"), such as [joy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joy "Joy"), [interest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interest_(emotion) "Interest (emotion)") or [contentment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contentment "Contentment"), contrast with those perceived as [unpleasant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suffering "Suffering"), like [anxiety](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anxiety "Anxiety"), [sadness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sadness "Sadness"), [anger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anger "Anger"), and [despair](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Depression_(mood) "Depression (mood)").[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-334)[Happiness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Happiness "Happiness"), or the state of being happy, is a human emotional condition. The definition of happiness is a common philosophical topic. Some define it as experiencing the [feeling](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feeling "Feeling") of positive [emotional affects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affect_(psychology) "Affect (psychology)"), while avoiding the negative ones.[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-335)[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-336) Others see it as an appraisal of [life satisfaction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_satisfaction "Life satisfaction") or [quality of life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quality_of_life "Quality of life").[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-337) Recent research suggests that being happy might involve experiencing some negative emotions when humans feel they are warranted.[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-338)

### Sexuality and love

Main articles: [Human sexuality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_sexuality "Human sexuality") and [Love](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Love "Love")

[![Image 36](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Sweet_Baby_Kisses_Family_Love.jpg/250px-Sweet_Baby_Kisses_Family_Love.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sweet_Baby_Kisses_Family_Love.jpg)

Human parents often display [familial love](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Familial_love "Familial love") for their children.

For humans, sexuality involves [biological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological "Biological"), [erotic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Erotic "Erotic"), [physical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physical_intimacy "Physical intimacy"), [emotional](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emotional_intimacy "Emotional intimacy"), [social](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social "Social"), or [spiritual](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spirituality "Spirituality") feelings and behaviors.[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-S._Greenberg-339)[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bolin-340) Because it is a broad term, which has varied with historical contexts over time, it lacks a precise definition.[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bolin-340) The biological and physical aspects of sexuality largely concern the [human reproductive functions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_reproduction "Human reproduction"), including the [human sexual response cycle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_sexual_response_cycle "Human sexual response cycle").[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-S._Greenberg-339)[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bolin-340) Sexuality also affects and is affected by cultural, political, legal, philosophical, [moral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morality "Morality"), [ethical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethical "Ethical"), and religious aspects of life.[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-S._Greenberg-339)[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bolin-340) Sexual desire, or _[libido](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libido "Libido")_, is a basic mental state present at the beginning of sexual behavior. Studies show that men desire sex more than women and [masturbate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masturbation "Masturbation") more often.[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-341)

Humans can fall anywhere along a continuous scale of [sexual orientation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_orientation "Sexual orientation"),[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-342) although most humans are [heterosexual](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heterosexual "Heterosexual").[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bailey16-343)[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-LeVay-344) While [homosexual](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homosexuality "Homosexuality") behavior [occurs in some other animals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homosexual_behavior_in_animals "Homosexual behavior in animals"), only humans and [domestic sheep](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheep "Sheep") have so far been found to exhibit exclusive preference for same-sex relationships.[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bailey16-343) Most evidence supports nonsocial, [biological causes of sexual orientation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology_and_sexual_orientation "Biology and sexual orientation"),[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bailey16-343) as cultures that are very tolerant of homosexuality do not have significantly higher rates of it.[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-LeVay-344)[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-345) Research in [neuroscience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroscience "Neuroscience") and [genetics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genetics "Genetics") suggests that other aspects of human sexuality are biologically influenced as well.[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-346)

Love most commonly refers to a feeling of strong attraction or emotional [attachment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attachment_(psychology) "Attachment (psychology)"). It can be impersonal (the love of an object, ideal, or strong political or spiritual connection) or interpersonal (love between humans).[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-347) When in love [dopamine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dopamine "Dopamine"), [norepinephrine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norepinephrine "Norepinephrine"), [serotonin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serotonin "Serotonin") and other chemicals stimulate the brain's [pleasure center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pleasure_center "Pleasure center"), leading to side effects such as increased [heart rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heart_rate "Heart rate"), loss of [appetite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anorexia_(symptom) "Anorexia (symptom)") and [sleep](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insomnia "Insomnia"), and an [intense feeling of excitement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euphoria "Euphoria").[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-348)

Culture
-------

Main articles: [Culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture "Culture") and [Cultural universal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_universal "Cultural universal")

Human society statistics| Most widely spoken languages[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-349)[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-CIAWorldFactbook-350) | [English](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language "English language"), [Mandarin Chinese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese "Mandarin Chinese"), [Hindi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindi "Hindi"), [Spanish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_language "Spanish language"), [Standard Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_Arabic "Standard Arabic"), [Bengali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bengali_language "Bengali language"), [French](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language "French language"), [Russian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_language "Russian language"), [Portuguese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Portuguese_language "Portuguese language"), [Urdu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urdu "Urdu") |
| --- |
| Most practiced religions[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-CIAWorldFactbook-350)[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-351) | [Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity "Christianity"), [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam"), [Hinduism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hinduism "Hinduism"), [Buddhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism"), [folk religions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folk_religion "Folk religion"), [Sikhism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sikhism "Sikhism"), [Judaism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judaism "Judaism"), [unaffiliated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irreligion "Irreligion") |

Humanity's unprecedented set of intellectual skills were a key factor in the species' eventual technological advancement and concomitant domination of the biosphere.[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-352) Disregarding extinct hominids, humans are the only animals known to teach generalizable information,[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-353) innately deploy recursive [embedding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dependent_clause "Dependent clause") to generate and communicate complex concepts,[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-354) engage in the "[folk physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Folk_physics "Folk physics")" required for competent tool design,[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-355)[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-356) or cook food in the wild.[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-357) Teaching and learning preserves the cultural and ethnographic identity of human societies.[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-358) Other traits and behaviors that are mostly unique to humans include starting fires,[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-359)[phoneme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phoneme "Phoneme") structuring[[357]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-360) and [vocal learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vocal_learning "Vocal learning").[[358]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-361)

### Language

Main article: [Language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language "Language")

[![Image 37](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Primary_Human_Languages_Improved_Version.png/500px-Primary_Human_Languages_Improved_Version.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Primary_Human_Languages_Improved_Version.png)

Principal [language families](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_language_families "List of language families") of the world (and in some cases geographic groups of families).

While many species [communicate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Animal_communication "Animal communication"), [language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language "Language") is unique to humans, a defining feature of humanity, and a [cultural universal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_universal "Cultural universal").[[359]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-362) Unlike the limited systems of other animals, human language is open– an infinite number of meanings can be produced by combining a limited number of symbols.[[360]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-363)[[361]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-364) Human language also has the capacity of [displacement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Displacement_(linguistics) "Displacement (linguistics)"), using words to represent things and happenings that are not presently or locally occurring but reside in the shared imagination of interlocutors.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Revolution-155)

Language differs from other forms of communication in that it is [modality independent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origin_of_speech#Modality-independence "Origin of speech"); the same meanings can be conveyed through different media, audibly in [speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speech "Speech"), visually by [sign language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sign_language "Sign language") or writing, and through tactile media such as [braille](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille "Braille").[[362]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-365) Language is central to the communication between humans, and to the sense of identity that unites nations, cultures and ethnic groups.[[363]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-366) There are approximately six thousand different languages currently in use, including sign languages, and many thousands more that are [extinct](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extinct_language "Extinct language").[[364]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-367)

### The arts

Main article: [The arts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_arts "The arts")

Human arts can take many forms including [visual](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visual_arts "Visual arts"), [literary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literary_arts "Literary arts"), and [performing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Performing_arts "Performing arts"). Visual art can range from [paintings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Painting "Painting") and [sculptures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sculpture "Sculpture") to [film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Film "Film"), [fashion design](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fashion_design "Fashion design"), and [architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Architecture "Architecture").[[365]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-368) Literary arts can include [prose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prose "Prose"), [poetry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poetry "Poetry"), and [dramas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drama "Drama"). The performing arts generally involve [theatre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theatre "Theatre"), [music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music "Music"), and [dance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dance "Dance").[[366]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-369)[[367]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-370) Humans often combine the different forms (for example, music videos).[[368]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-371) Other entities that have been described as having artistic qualities include [food preparation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culinary_arts "Culinary arts"), [video games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Video_game "Video game"), and [medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicine "Medicine").[[369]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-372)[[370]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-373)[[371]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-374) As well as providing entertainment and transferring knowledge, the arts are also used for [political purposes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_arts_and_politics "The arts and politics").[[372]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-375)

[![Image 38](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/British_Museum_Flood_Tablet.jpg/250px-British_Museum_Flood_Tablet.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:British_Museum_Flood_Tablet.jpg)

The [Deluge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deluge_(mythology) "Deluge (mythology)") tablet of [the _Gilgamesh_ epic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epic_of_Gilgamesh "Epic of Gilgamesh") in [Akkadian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Akkadian_language "Akkadian language")

[Art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Art "Art") is a defining characteristic of humans and there is evidence for a relationship between creativity and language.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Morriss-Kay-2010-376) The earliest evidence of art was shell engravings made by _Homo erectus_ 300,000 years before modern humans evolved.[[374]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-377) Art attributed to _H. sapiens_ existed at least 75,000 years ago, with jewellery and drawings found in caves in South Africa.[[375]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-378)[[376]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-379) There are various hypotheses as to why humans have [adapted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adaptation "Adaptation") to the arts. These include allowing them to better problem solve issues, providing a means to control or influence other humans, encouraging cooperation and contribution within a society or increasing the chance of attracting a potential mate.[[377]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-380) The use of imagination developed through art, combined with logic may have given early humans an evolutionary advantage.[[373]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Morriss-Kay-2010-376)

Evidence of humans engaging in musical activities predates cave art and so far music has been [practiced by virtually all known human cultures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_universal "Cultural universal").[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Morley-2014-381) There exists a wide variety of [music genres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_genre "Music genre") and [ethnic musics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_music "Ethnic music"); with humans' musical abilities being related to other abilities, including complex social human behaviours.[[378]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Morley-2014-381) It has been shown that human brains respond to music by becoming synchronized with the rhythm and beat, a process called [entrainment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entrainment_(biomusicology) "Entrainment (biomusicology)").[[379]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-382) Dance is also a form of human expression found in all cultures[[380]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-383) and may have evolved as a way to help early humans communicate.[[381]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-384) Listening to music and observing dance stimulates the [orbitofrontal cortex](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orbitofrontal_cortex "Orbitofrontal cortex") and other pleasure sensing areas of the brain.[[382]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-385)

Unlike speaking, reading and writing does not come naturally to humans and must be taught.[[383]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-386) Still, [literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literature "Literature") has been present before the invention of words and language, with 30,000-year-old paintings on walls inside some caves portraying a series of dramatic scenes.[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Puchner-387) One of the oldest surviving works of literature is the _[Epic of Gilgamesh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epic\_of\_Gilgamesh "Epic of Gilgamesh")_, first engraved on ancient [Babylonian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Babylonia "Babylonia") tablets about 4,000 years ago.[[385]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-388) Beyond simply passing down knowledge, the use and sharing of imaginative [fiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiction "Fiction") through stories might have helped develop humans' capabilities for communication and increased the likelihood of securing a mate.[[386]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-389) Storytelling may also be used as a way to provide the audience with moral lessons and encourage cooperation.[[384]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Puchner-387)

### Tools and technologies

Main articles: [Tool](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tool "Tool") and [Technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technology "Technology")

[![Image 39: Train running on a track](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/JR-Maglev-MLX01-2.jpg/250px-JR-Maglev-MLX01-2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:JR-Maglev-MLX01-2.jpg)

The [SCMaglev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SCMaglev "SCMaglev"), the [fastest train](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Land_speed_record_for_rail_vehicles "Land speed record for rail vehicles") in the world clocking in at 603 km/h (375 mph) as of 2015[[387]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-390)

Stone tools were used by proto-humans at least 2.5 million years ago.[[388]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-391) The use and manufacture of tools has been put forward as the ability that defines humans more than anything else[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Choi-2009-392) and has historically been seen as an important evolutionary step.[[390]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-393) The technology became much more sophisticated about 1.8 million years ago,[[389]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Choi-2009-392) with the [controlled use of fire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Control_of_fire_by_early_humans "Control of fire by early humans") beginning around 1 million years ago.[[391]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-394)[[392]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-395) The wheel and wheeled vehicles appeared simultaneously in several regions some time in the fourth millennium BC.[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Bodn%C3%A1r-2018-65) The development of more complex tools and technologies allowed land to be [cultivated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arable_land "Arable land") and animals to be [domesticated](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestication "Domestication"), thus proving essential in the development of [agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agriculture "Agriculture")– what is known as the [Neolithic Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution "Neolithic Revolution").[[393]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-396)

[China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China") developed [paper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paper "Paper"), the [printing press](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Printing_press "Printing press"), [gunpowder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gunpowder "Gunpowder"), the [compass](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compass "Compass") and [other important inventions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Chinese_inventions "List of Chinese inventions").[[394]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-397) The continued improvements in [smelting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smelting "Smelting") allowed [forging](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Forging "Forging") of copper, bronze, iron and eventually [steel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steel "Steel"), which is used in [railways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Railways "Railways"), [skyscrapers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skyscraper "Skyscraper") and many other products.[[395]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-398) This coincided with the [Industrial Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_Revolution "Industrial Revolution"), where the invention of automated machines brought major changes to humans' lifestyles.[[396]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-399) Modern technology is observed as [progressing exponentially](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accelerating_change "Accelerating change"),[[397]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-400) with major innovations in the 20th century including: [electricity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electricity_generation "Electricity generation"), [penicillin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Penicillin "Penicillin"), [semiconductors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semiconductor "Semiconductor"), [internal combustion engines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_combustion_engine "Internal combustion engine"), the [Internet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet "Internet"), [nitrogen fixing fertilizers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fertilizer "Fertilizer"), [airplanes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airplane "Airplane"), [computers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer "Computer"), [automobiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Car "Car"), [contraceptive pills](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Combined_oral_contraceptive_pill "Combined oral contraceptive pill"), [nuclear fission](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_fission "Nuclear fission"), the [green revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Revolution "Green Revolution"), [radio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio "Radio"), scientific [plant breeding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plant_breeding "Plant breeding"), [rockets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rocket "Rocket"), [air conditioning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Air_conditioning "Air conditioning"), [television](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Television "Television") and the [assembly line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assembly_line "Assembly line").[[398]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-401)

### Religion and spirituality

Main articles: [Religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion "Religion") and [Spirituality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spirituality "Spirituality")

[![Image 40](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Brooklyn_Museum_1992.133.4_Figure_of_Shango_on_Horseback.jpg/250px-Brooklyn_Museum_1992.133.4_Figure_of_Shango_on_Horseback.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Brooklyn_Museum_1992.133.4_Figure_of_Shango_on_Horseback.jpg)

[Shango](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shango "Shango"), the [Orisha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orisha "Orisha") of fire, lightning, and thunder, in the [Yoruba religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yoruba_religion "Yoruba religion"), depicted on horseback

[Definitions of religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Definition_of_religion "Definition of religion") vary;[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Idinopulos-1998-402) according to one definition, a religion is a [belief](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Belief "Belief") system concerning the [supernatural](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supernatural "Supernatural"), [sacred](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sacred "Sacred") or [divine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Divinity "Divinity"), and practices, [values](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Values "Values"), institutions and [rituals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ritual "Ritual") associated with such belief. Some religions also have a [moral code](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moral_code "Moral code"). The [evolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_psychology_of_religion "Evolutionary psychology of religion") and the history of the [first religions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_origin_of_religions "Evolutionary origin of religions") have become areas of active scientific investigation.[[400]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-403)[[401]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-404)[[402]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-405) Credible evidence of religious behaviour dates to the [Middle Paleolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic "Middle Paleolithic") era (45–200 [thousand years ago](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tya_(unit) "Tya (unit)")).[[403]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-406) It may have evolved to play a role in helping enforce and encourage cooperation between humans.[[404]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-407)

Religion manifests in diverse forms.[[399]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Idinopulos-1998-402) Religion can include a belief in [life after death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_after_death "Life after death"),[[405]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-408) the [origin of life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origin_of_life "Origin of life"), the nature of the [universe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universe "Universe") ([religious cosmology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_cosmology "Religious cosmology")) and its [ultimate fate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultimate_fate "Ultimate fate") ([eschatology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eschatology "Eschatology")), and [moral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morality "Morality") or [ethical teachings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religious_ethics "Religious ethics").[[406]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-409) Views on [transcendence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcendence_(religion) "Transcendence (religion)") and [immanence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immanence "Immanence") vary substantially; traditions variously espouse [monism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monism "Monism"), [deism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deism "Deism"), [pantheism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pantheism "Pantheism"), and [theism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theism "Theism") (including [polytheism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polytheism "Polytheism") and [monotheism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monotheism "Monotheism")).[[407]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-410)

Although measuring religiosity is difficult,[[408]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-411) a majority of humans profess some variety of religious or spiritual belief.[[409]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-412) In 2015 the plurality were [Christian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christians "Christians") followed by [Muslims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslims "Muslims"), [Hindus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hindus "Hindus") and [Buddhists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism").[[410]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-413) As of 2015, about 16%, or slightly under 1.2 billion humans, were [irreligious](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irreligious "Irreligious"), including those with no religious beliefs or no identity with any religion.[[411]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-414)

### Science and philosophy

Main articles: [Science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science "Science") and [Philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy "Philosophy")

[![Image 41](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Dunhuang_star_map.jpg/250px-Dunhuang_star_map.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dunhuang_star_map.jpg)

The [Dunhuang map](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dunhuang_map "Dunhuang map"), a [star map](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_map "Star map") showing the North Polar region. China circa 700.

An aspect unique to humans is their ability to [transmit knowledge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_transfer "Knowledge transfer") from one generation to the next and to continually build on this information to develop tools, [scientific laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_law "Scientific law") and other advances to pass on further.[[412]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-415) This accumulated knowledge can be tested to answer questions or make predictions about how the universe functions and has been very successful in advancing human ascendancy.[[413]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-416)

[Aristotle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotle "Aristotle") has been described as the first scientist,[[414]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-417) and preceded the rise of scientific thought through the [Hellenistic period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hellenistic_period "Hellenistic period").[[415]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-418) Other early advances in science came from the [Han dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_and_technology_of_the_Han_dynasty "Science and technology of the Han dynasty") in China and during the [Islamic Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age "Islamic Golden Age").[[416]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-419)[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Renima-2016-91) The [scientific revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_Revolution "Scientific Revolution"), near the end of the [Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance "Renaissance"), led to the emergence of [modern science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_science "Modern science").[[417]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-420)

A chain of events and influences led to the development of the [scientific method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific_method "Scientific method"), a process of observation and experimentation that is used to differentiate science from [pseudoscience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pseudoscience "Pseudoscience").[[418]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-421) An understanding of [mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics "Mathematics") is unique to humans, although other species of animals have some [numerical cognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Numerical_cognition "Numerical cognition").[[419]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-422) All of science can be divided into three major branches, the [formal sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_sciences "Formal sciences") (e.g., [logic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic "Logic") and [mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics "Mathematics")), which are concerned with [formal systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Formal_systems "Formal systems"), the [applied sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Applied_sciences "Applied sciences") (e.g., engineering, medicine), which are focused on practical applications, and the empirical sciences, which are based on [empirical observation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empirical_observation "Empirical observation") and are in turn divided into [natural sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_sciences "Natural sciences") (e.g., [physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physics "Physics"), [chemistry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemistry "Chemistry"), [biology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biology "Biology")) and [social sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_sciences "Social sciences") (e.g., [psychology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology "Psychology"), economics, sociology).[[420]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-423)

Philosophy is a field of study where humans seek to understand fundamental truths about themselves and the world in which they live.[[421]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-424) Philosophical inquiry has been a major feature in the development of humans' intellectual history.[[422]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-425) It has been described as the "no man's land" between definitive scientific knowledge and dogmatic religious teachings.[[423]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-426) Major fields of philosophy include [metaphysics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metaphysics "Metaphysics"), [epistemology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epistemology "Epistemology"), [logic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logic_(philosophy) "Logic (philosophy)"), and [axiology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axiology "Axiology") (which includes [ethics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethics "Ethics") and [aesthetics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aesthetics "Aesthetics")).[[424]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-427)

Society
-------

Main article: [Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society "Society")

[![Image 42](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Indian_family_in_Brazil_posed_in_front_of_hut.jpg/250px-Indian_family_in_Brazil_posed_in_front_of_hut.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Indian_family_in_Brazil_posed_in_front_of_hut.jpg)

Humans often live in family-based social structures.

Society is the system of organizations and institutions arising from interaction between humans. Humans are highly social and tend to live in large complex social groups. They can be divided into different groups according to their income, wealth, [power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_(social_and_political) "Power (social and political)"), [reputation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reputation "Reputation") and other factors. The structure of [social stratification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_stratification "Social stratification") and the degree of [social mobility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_mobility "Social mobility") differs, especially between modern and traditional societies.[[425]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-428) Human groups range from the size of [families](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family "Family") to nations. The first form of human social organization is thought to have resembled [hunter-gatherer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunter-gatherer "Hunter-gatherer")[band societies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Band_society "Band society").[[426]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-429)

### Gender

Main article: [Gender](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender "Gender")

[![Image 43](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Human.svg/250px-Human.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Human.svg)

Depiction of a [man](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man "Man") and a [woman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woman "Woman") from the [Pioneer plaque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pioneer_plaque "Pioneer plaque")

Human societies typically exhibit [gender identities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_identity "Gender identity") and [gender roles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_role "Gender role") that distinguish between [masculine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masculinity "Masculinity") and [feminine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Femininity "Femininity") characteristics and prescribe the range of acceptable behaviours and attitudes for their members based on their sex.[[427]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-430)[[428]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-431) The most common categorisation is a [gender binary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gender_binary "Gender binary") of [men](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Men "Men") and [women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women "Women").[[429]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-432) Some societies recognize a [third gender](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Third_gender "Third gender"),[[430]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-433) or less commonly a fourth or fifth.[[431]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-434)[[432]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-435) In some other societies, [non-binary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-binary_gender "Non-binary gender") is used as an umbrella term for a range of gender identities that are not solely male or female.[[433]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-436)

Gender roles are often associated with a division of [norms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_norm "Social norm"), [practices](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Practice_(social_theory) "Practice (social theory)"), [dress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clothing "Clothing"), [behavior](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_behavior "Social behavior"), [rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rights "Rights"), [duties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duty "Duty"), [privileges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privilege_(social_inequality) "Privilege (social inequality)"), [status](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_status "Social status"), and [power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_(social_and_political) "Power (social and political)"), with men enjoying more rights and privileges than women in most societies, both today and in the past.[[434]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-437) As a [social construct](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_constructionism "Social constructionism"),[[435]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-438) gender roles are not fixed and vary historically within a society. Challenges to predominant gender norms have recurred in many societies.[[436]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-439)[[437]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-440) Little is known about gender roles in the earliest human societies. [Early modern humans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Early_modern_human "Early modern human") probably had a range of gender roles similar to that of modern cultures from at least the [Upper Paleolithic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Paleolithic "Upper Paleolithic"), while the Neanderthals were less sexually dimorphic and there is evidence that the behavioural difference between males and females was minimal.[[438]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-441)

### Kinship

Main article: [Kinship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinship "Kinship")

All human societies organize, recognize and classify types of social relationships based on relations between parents, children and other descendants ([consanguinity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consanguinity "Consanguinity")), and relations through [marriage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marriage "Marriage") ([affinity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Affinity_(law) "Affinity (law)")). There is also a third type applied to [godparents](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Godparent "Godparent") or [adoptive children](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adoption "Adoption") ([fictive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fictive_kinship "Fictive kinship")). These culturally defined relationships are referred to as kinship. In many societies, it is one of the most important social organizing principles and plays a role in transmitting status and [inheritance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inheritance "Inheritance").[[439]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-442)All societies have rules of [incest taboo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incest_taboo "Incest taboo"), according to which marriage between certain kinds of kin relations is prohibited, and some also have rules of preferential marriage with certain kin relations.[[440]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-443)

Pair bonding is a ubiquitous feature of human sexual relationships, whether it is manifested as serial monogamy, [polygyny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polygyny "Polygyny"), or [polyandry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polyandry "Polyandry").[[441]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-444) Genetic evidence indicates that humans were predominantly [polygynous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polygyny "Polygyny") for most of their existence as a species, but that this began to shift during the Neolithic, when [monogamy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monogamy "Monogamy") started becoming widespread concomitantly with the transition from nomadic to sedentary societies.[[442]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-445) Anatomical evidence in the form of second-to-fourth digit ratios, a biomarker for prenatal androgen effects, likewise indicates modern humans were polygynous during the Pleistocene.[[443]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-446)

### Ethnicity

Main article: [Ethnic group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_group "Ethnic group")

Human ethnic groups are a social category that [identifies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Identity_(social_science) "Identity (social science)") together as a group based on shared attributes that distinguish them from other groups. These can be a common set of traditions, [ancestry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancestry "Ancestry"), [language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Language "Language"), [history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History "History"), [society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Society "Society"), [culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture "Culture"), [nation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation "Nation"), [religion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion "Religion"), or social treatment within their residing area.[[444]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-447)[[445]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-448) Ethnicity is separate from the concept of [race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_(human_categorization) "Race (human categorization)"), which is based on physical characteristics, although both are [socially constructed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_constructionism "Social constructionism").[[446]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-449) Assigning ethnicity to a certain population is complicated, as even within common ethnic designations there can be a diverse range of subgroups, and the makeup of these ethnic groups can change over time at both the collective and individual level.[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-REGWG2005-181) Also, there is no generally accepted definition of what constitutes an ethnic group.[[447]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-450) Ethnic groupings can play a powerful role in the [social identity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_identity "Social identity") and solidarity of ethnopolitical units. This has been closely tied to the rise of the [nation state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation_state "Nation state") as the predominant form of political organization in the 19th and 20th centuries.[[448]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-451)[[449]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-452)[[450]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-453)

### Government and politics

Main articles: [Government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government "Government") and [Politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics "Politics")

[![Image 44](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg/250px-United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City%2C_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:United_Nations_Headquarters_in_New_York_City,_view_from_Roosevelt_Island.jpg)
