The [United Nations headquarters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations "Headquarters of the United Nations") (left) in New York City, which houses one of the world's largest political organizations

As farming populations gathered in larger and denser communities, interactions between these different groups increased. This led to the development of governance within and between the communities.[[451]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-454) Humans have evolved the ability to change affiliation with various social groups relatively easily, including previously strong political alliances, if doing so is seen as providing personal advantages.[[452]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-455) This [cognitive flexibility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognitive_flexibility "Cognitive flexibility") allows individual humans to change their political ideologies, with those with higher flexibility less likely to support authoritarian and nationalistic stances.[[453]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-456)

Governments create [laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law "Law") and [policies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Policies "Policies") that affect the citizens that they govern. There have been [many forms of government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_forms_of_government "List of forms of government") throughout human history, each having various means of obtaining power and the ability to exert diverse controls on the population.[[454]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-457) Approximately 47% of humans live in some form of a [democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy "Democracy"), 17% in a [hybrid regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hybrid_regime "Hybrid regime"), and 37% in an [authoritarian regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_regime "Authoritarian regime").[[455]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-458) Many countries belong to [international organizations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_organization "International organization") and [alliances](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alliances "Alliances"); the largest of these is the [United Nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Nations "United Nations"), with [193 member states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations "Member states of the United Nations").[[456]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-459)

### Trade and economics

Main articles: [Trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade "Trade") and [Economics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economics "Economics")

[![Image 45](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Silk_route.jpg/330px-Silk_route.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Silk_route.jpg)

The [Silk Road](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silk_Road "Silk Road") (red) and spice [trade routes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_routes "Trade routes") (blue)

Trade, the voluntary exchange of goods and services, is seen as a characteristic that differentiates humans from other animals and has been cited as a practice that gave _Homo sapiens_ a major advantage over other hominids.[[457]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-460) Evidence suggests early _H. sapiens_ made use of long-distance trade routes to exchange goods and ideas, leading to [cultural explosions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_explosion "Cultural explosion") and providing additional food sources when hunting was sparse, while such trade networks did not exist for the now extinct Neanderthals.[[458]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-461)[[459]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-462) Early trade likely involved materials for creating tools like [obsidian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Obsidian "Obsidian").[[460]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-463) The first truly international trade routes were around the [spice trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spice_trade "Spice trade") through the Roman and medieval periods.[[461]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-464)

Early human [economies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy "Economy") were more likely to be based around [gift giving](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gift_economy "Gift economy") instead of a [bartering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barter "Barter") system.[[462]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-465) Early [money](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Money "Money") consisted of [commodities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commodity_money "Commodity money"); the oldest being in the form of cattle and the most widely used being [cowrie shells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cowrie_shells "Cowrie shells").[[463]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-www.pbs.org-1996-466) Money has since evolved into governmental issued [coins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coins "Coins"), [paper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paper_money "Paper money") and [electronic money](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronic_money "Electronic money").[[463]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-www.pbs.org-1996-466) Human study of economics is a [social science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_science "Social science") that looks at how societies distribute scarce resources among different people.[[464]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-467) There are massive [inequalities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_inequality "Economic inequality") in the division of [wealth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wealth "Wealth") among humans; the eight richest humans are worth the same monetary value as the poorest half of all the human population.[[465]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-468)

### Conflict

Main article: [Conflict (process)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conflict_(process) "Conflict (process)")

Further information: [Violent crime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Violent_crime "Violent crime") and [War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War "War")

[![Image 46](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Into_the_Jaws_of_Death_23-0455M_edit.jpg/250px-Into_the_Jaws_of_Death_23-0455M_edit.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Into_the_Jaws_of_Death_23-0455M_edit.jpg)

American troops [landing at Normandy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Normandy_landings "Normandy landings"), WWII

Humans commit violence on other humans at a rate comparable to other primates, but have an increased preference for killing adults, [infanticide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infanticide_(zoology) "Infanticide (zoology)") being more common among other primates.[[466]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-469) Phylogenetic analysis predicts that 2% of early _H. sapiens_ would be [murdered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murder "Murder"), rising to 12% during the medieval period, before dropping to below 2% in modern times.[[467]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-470) There is great variation in violence between human populations, with rates of homicide about 0.01% in societies that have [legal systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_national_legal_systems "List of national legal systems") and strong cultural attitudes against violence.[[468]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-471)

The willingness of humans to kill other members of their species en masse through organized conflict (i.e., [war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War "War")) has long been the subject of debate. One school of thought holds that war evolved as a means to eliminate competitors, and has always been an innate human characteristic. Another suggests that war is a relatively recent phenomenon and has appeared due to changing social conditions.[[469]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Ferguson-2018-472) While not settled, current evidence indicates warlike predispositions only became common about 10,000 years ago, and in many places much more recently than that.[[469]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-Ferguson-2018-472) War has had a high cost on human life; it is estimated that during the 20th century, between 167 million and 188 million people died as a result of war.[[470]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-473) War casualty data is less reliable for pre-medieval times, especially global figures. But compared with any period over the past 600 years, the last 80 years (post 1946) has seen a very significant drop in global military and civilian death rates due to armed conflict.[[471]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_note-474)

The changes that occur during puberty usually happen in an ordered sequence, beginning with thelarche (breast development) at around age 10 or 11, followed by adrenarche (growth of pubic hair due to androgen stimulation), peak height velocity, and finally menarche (the onset of menses), which usually occurs around age 12 or 13.

On average, the onset of puberty is about 18 months earlier for girls (usually starting around the age of 10 or 11 and lasting until they are 15 to 17) than for boys (who usually begin puberty at about the age of 11 to 12 and complete it by the age of 16 to 17, on average).

333.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_ref-336)**Haybron DM (13 April 2014). I would suggest that when we talk about happiness, we are actually referring, much of the time, to a complex emotional phenomenon. Call it emotional well-being. Happiness as emotional well-being concerns your emotions and moods, more broadly your emotional condition as a whole. To be happy is to inhabit a favorable emotional state.... On this view, we can think of happiness, loosely, as the opposite of anxiety and depression. Being in good spirits, quick to laugh and slow to anger, at peace and untroubled, confident and comfortable in your own skin, engaged, energetic and full of life.

445.   **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human#cite_ref-448)**People J, Bailey G (2010). _Humanity: An Introduction to Cultural Anthropology_ (9th ed.). Wadsworth Cengage learning. p.389. In essence, an ethnic group is a named social category of people based on perceptions of shared social experience or one's ancestors' experiences. Members of the ethnic group see themselves as sharing cultural traditions and history that distinguish them from other groups. Ethnic group identity has a strong psychological or emotional component that divides the people of the world into opposing categories of 'us' and 'them.' In contrast to social stratification, which divides and unifies people along a series of horizontal axes based on socioeconomic factors, ethnic identities divide and unify people along a series of vertical axes. Thus, ethnic groups, at least theoretically, cut across socioeconomic class differences, drawing members from all strata of the population.
